## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration (dA_dt) as a function of time and current concentration. Classical chemical kinetics relates reaction rates to concentration through rate laws (power-law, Michaelis-Menten, etc.), and time may appear explicitly in cases of time-dependent forcing or oscillatory reactions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, simple decomposition)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with reverse reaction from product at equilibrium offset)
- Mixed order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction)
- Logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * A) (growth with self-limitation, autocatalysis with inhibition)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (general polynomial expansion of rate)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Fractional order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Oscillatory forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodically driven reaction system)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservation laws in closed systems → rate expressions that sum to zero across species, implying dA_dt often has the form of a polynomial in A with roots at equilibrium concentrations
- Stoichiometric constraints → rate expressions involving integer or simple rational powers of concentration (A**1, A**2, A**3)
- Enzyme saturation → when rate plateaus at high concentration, Michaelis-Menten form c0*A/(c1+A) or Hill equation c0*A**c1/(c2+A**c1) is appropriate
- Equilibrium behavior → dA_dt must equal zero at steady-state concentration, so the expression should have a real root in A at the equilibrium value
- Mass-action kinetics → products of concentrations raised to stoichiometric coefficients; for single species, this yields pure power-law terms A**n
- Consecutive reactions → rate expressions involving differences of exponential terms in time, or sums of terms like c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*exp(c3*t)
- Autocatalytic feedback → presence of positive terms in A**2 or higher powers indicating self-accelerating behavior
- Detailed balance constraint → forward and reverse rate terms appear as separate additive contributions (e.g., c0*A**n - c1*A**m)
- Time-concentration separability → if the system is autonomous (most chemical kinetics), dA_dt should depend only on A, not explicitly on t

Setting c0=0, c1=0, c3=0, c7=0, c6=0: gives c4·sin(c5·A). Missing the √A term. A^(1/4) ≠ √A, so this can't produce √A. No match.

**Candidate 9: A^c0*c1*log(A*c2+1) + A^c3*c4*sin(A*c5+c6)**

Setting c0=0.5, c1 = -0.10017 (but this gives -0.10017·√A·... wait, the first term is c1·A^c0·log(c2·A+1)). The log term can't become √A. If we set c1=0 to kill the first term, we get A^c3·c4·sin(c5·A+c6). Setting c3=0.5 gives √A·c4·sin(c5·A+c6), which is √A·sin(...), not what we want (we need √A + sin(...)). No match.

**Candidate 10 is confirmed as a match.**

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: -0.10017·√A + 0.47149·sin(0.85551·A)**

The GT has exactly two terms: a `√A` term and a `sin(A)` term (with specific frequency). No polynomial terms, no exponential terms, no logarithmic terms, no `t` dependence.

- GT has `√A` and `sin(c·A)` as basis functions
- No constant term, no polynomial terms, no exponential terms, no log terms, no `t` terms
- Candidates with `A^(1/4)` cannot produce `√A` — these are different basis functions → NO MATCH
- Candidates with only polynomial + sin can match if all polynomial coefficients can be zeroed
